## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of (forced/damped) nonlinear oscillators. Typical physics includes restoring forces from a potential U(x), damping terms depending on v (possibly state-dependent), and optional external driving as explicit functions of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small oscillations near equilibrium; c0 typically negative, ~ -omega^2)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-spring-damper with linear drag; c1 typically negative)
- Constant/offset acceleration: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v (bias force or gravity-like offset plus linear terms)
- Quadratic (turbulent-like) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipation approximation)
- Cubic stiffness (Duffing backbone, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x^3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x^3 + c2 * x^5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring force for large amplitudes)
- Nonlinear damping (van der Pol form): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x^2) * v (self-excited or amplitude-dependent damping; e.g., (1 - x^2)v)
- Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v^3 (damping nonlinearity depending on velocity amplitude)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (periodic restoring torque; small-angle limit reduces to linear in x)
- Externally forced harmonic drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (periodic forcing of an oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator with forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x^3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (canonical forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric pumping)
- State-dependent forcing/coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x * cos(c3 * t) (multiplicative forcing via displacement-dependent modulation)
- Potential-gradient form: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x^2 + c4 * x^4) * x (dv_dt = damping + restoring derived from polynomial potential U(x))

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative spring-like restoring forces are often odd in x (terms like x, x^3, x^5), corresponding to an even potential U(x).
- Small-amplitude linearization: near equilibrium, nonlinear restoring terms reduce to dv_dt ≈ c0 * x (the leading Taylor term dominates).
- Dissipation signature: damping typically appears as terms proportional to v or functions multiplying v (e.g., (c0 + c1*x^2)*v); negative coefficients imply energy loss.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency shift: inclusion of x^3 (Duffing) commonly produces frequency that depends on oscillation amplitude; expect x and x^3 together.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: nonlinear damping of form (c0 + c1*x^2)*v with sign changes versus x can inject energy at small amplitudes and remove it at large amplitudes (van der Pol mechanism).
- Turbulent-like drag: terms v*Abs(v) capture direction-preserving quadratic drag and often dominate at high speeds compared with linear v damping.
- Periodic forcing: explicit dependence on t via sin/cos indicates external driving; expect resonance when forcing frequency matches the natural frequency implied by the x-term.
- Parametric resonance: time-varying stiffness (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x can destabilize the trivial solution and produce growth in oscillations even without additive forcing.
- Conservative vs forced/damped separation: if dv_dt contains only x (and possibly nonlinear functions of x) but no v and no explicit t, dynamics are conservative; adding v introduces dissipation, adding t introduces nonautonomous forcing.

\[
f(x,t,v)= -0.59954989233168\,v\;-\;2.79522534599104\,x\,e^{-|x|}.

So any matching candidate must be exactly “linear in \(v\)” plus “\(x\exp(k|x|)\)” with **the same** \(k=-1\), and **no** extra dependence on \(t\), no constants, no other \(x\)-only terms, no nonlinear \(v\) terms, etc. (Variables can be negative, so \(|x|\) cannot be dropped.)

### 1. `c0 + c1*v + c2*x*exp(c3*Abs(x)) + c4/(c5*t + c6) + t/(c5*t + c6)`
To match GT, all \(t\)-dependent rational terms must vanish. But \(t/(c5 t+c6)\) cannot be made identically 0 for all \(t\) by choosing constants (unless you allow an invalid “denominator → ∞” trick). So cannot match. **No.**

### 2. `c0*x*exp(c1*Abs(x)) + c2*v + c3 + c4*log(c5*t + 1) + v`
Has extra `+ v` (so \(v\)-coefficient is \(c2+1\), that’s fine), but also constant \(c3\) and \(t\)-dependent log term. Log term can be killed by \(c4=0\). Constant can be killed by \(c3=0\). Then we can set:
- \(c2+1=-0.5995498923\Rightarrow c2=-1.5995498923\)
- \(c1=-1\)
- \(c0=-2.79522534599\)
This yields exactly GT. **Yes, match possible.**

### 3. `c0*v + c1*x*exp(c2*Abs(x)) + c3*exp(c4*x)`
Extra term \(c3 e^{c4 x}\). Only way to remove for all \(x\) is \(c3=0\). Then set \(c0=-0.5995498923\), \(c2=-1\), \(c1=-2.79522534599\). **Yes.**

### 4. `c0*v + c1*x*exp(c2*Abs(x)) + c3*cos(c4*log(c5*exp(c6*t + c7*x) + 1))`

### 6. `c0*x*exp(c1*Abs(x)) + c2*v + c3 + c4*x**c5*exp(c6*Abs(v)) + v`

**Candidate 1:** `c0 + c1*v + c2*x*exp(c3*Abs(x)) + c4/(c5*t + c6) + t/(c5*t + c6)`
